# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Kubernetes Server-Side Apply Configuration Guide

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a deep guide for applyconfigurations and Server-Side Apply semantics, including conflict handling and workflow patterns.

## Scope

Focus on the applyconfigurations and Server-Side Apply subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

The documentation has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what it covers:

**Structure:**
1. **Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries** — What SSA does, what it does not (no strategic merge patch on apply), and where it sits relative to the HTTP layer and etcd.

2. **Key Components and Responsibility Split** — The `Manager` interface, the `FieldManager` facade, and the full decorator chain with one row per decorator explaining its file and purpose. Covers `TypeConverter`, `structuredMergeManager`, the HTTP handler `applyPatcher`, and the `applyconfigurations` client library.

3. **End-to-End Request Flow** — A concrete, nine-step trace from a client-side `Apply()` call through YAML parsing, the optimistic-concurrency retry loop, the Manager decorator chain (with call-order detail), conflict conversion, managed-field encoding, and the no-op apply timestamp suppressor.

4. **Conflict Handling** — What triggers a conflict at the `structured-merge-diff` layer, the exact HTTP response format with `FieldManagerConflict` cause types, and all four resolution strategies (force, field removal, coordination, CSA upgrade).

5. **Field Ownership Model** — The `ManagedFieldsEntry` wire format, the JSON manager-identifier key scheme that differs between Apply and Update managers, and the `FieldsV1` trie structure.

6. **Operational Implications** — Per-request conversion cost, managed-fields size growth and the etcd-size fallback that strips `managedFields` from non-apply requests, the no-op apply optimization and its CPU cost, `UpdateNoErrors` silent data loss, and the probabilistic create-tracking knob.

7. **Extension Points** — Custom field manager names, `resetFields`/`IgnoreFilter`, `ScaleHandler` for subresource path translation, CRD FieldManager diffe
... (truncated)

{
  "content": "# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and ApplyConfigurations: A Deep Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is a Kubernetes API mechanism introduced to replace the\nclient-side `kubectl apply` workflow with a server-enforced, field-ownership\nmodel. Instead of the client computing a three-way diff and sending a strategic\nmerge patch, the client sends a _declarative intent_\u2014a partial object\u2014and the\nserver is responsible for merging it with the live object, tracking ownership of\neach field, and detecting conflicts between competing actors.\n\n**What the subsystem does:**\n\n- Accepts apply requests (`PATCH` with `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml`)\n  and merge-patch/update requests.\n- Determines which fields are owned by which _field manager_ (identified by the\n  `fieldManager` query parameter) and records ownership in\n  `metadata.managedFields`.\n- Detects conflicts\u2014when two managers claim the same field with different\n  intended values\u2014and either returns a `409 Conflict` or forces through the\n  change when `force=true`.\n- Prunes fields that a manager previously owned but no longer declares in its\n  applied configuration.\n- Maintains backward compatibility with the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration`\n  annotation used by client-side apply.\n\n**Boundaries:**\n\n- The subsystem lives within the API server. The client's only job is to\n  produce an _apply configuration_\u2014a partial, pointer-heavy struct representation\n  of the intended object state.\n- Upstream: HTTP routing in `pkg/endpoints` passes PATCH requests to\n  `PatchResource` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`.\n- Downstream: After field management completes, the resulting object is\n  validated by admission webhooks and written to etcd via the registry layer.\n- Out of scope: The strategic merge patch algorithm used by classical `kubectl apply`\n  (client-side apply) is an entirely separate code path and does not run for SSA requests.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\nThe SSA subsystem is layered across three staging modules:\n\n| Module | Responsibility |\n|---|---|\n| `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields` | Core FieldManager orchestrator and public API |\n| `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal` | The actual merge/tracking logic, implemented as a chain of Manager decorators |\n| `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers` | HTTP entry point; ties FieldManager into the patch handler |\n| `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager` | Admission validation and noop-timestamp optimization |\n| `k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations` | Generated client-side types used to build apply requests |\n| `k8s.io/client-go/util/csaupgrade` | Utility for migrating CSA-managed objects to SSA |\n\n### 2.1 The `Manager` Interface\n\nThe central abstraction is the `Manager` interface in\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/manager.go`:\n\n```go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n    Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, fieldManager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n}\n```\n\n- **`Update`** is called for all non-apply write operations (PUT, strategic merge\n  patch, JSON patch). It only updates the field-ownership bookkeeping; the\n  object merge was already performed by the caller.\n- **`Apply`** is called for SSA requests. It both merges the applied configuration\n  into the live object and updates ownership.\n\nThe `Managed` interface (`manager.go`) groups a `fieldpath.ManagedFields` map\nfrom `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` with per-manager timestamps. This is\nthe in-memory representation of `metadata.managedFields`.\n\n### 2.2 The `FieldManager` Facade\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go`\nwraps a `Manager` chain and is the object exposed to the HTTP handler. Its\nexported methods:\n\n- `Update(liveObj, newObj, managerName)` \u2014 decodes managed fields from the\n  request, delegates to the chain, then re-encodes them back onto the result.\n- `Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, managerName, force)` \u2014 reads managed fields from\n  the live object (never from the applied patch, which must not contain them),\n  delegates to the chain, then re-encodes.\n- `UpdateNoErrors` \u2014 same as `Update` but swallows errors, clearing\n  `managedFields` rather than propagating the failure. Used for non-apply paths\n  where managed-field tracking is best-effort.\n\nThe public package `managedfields` (`fieldmanager.go` at the public level) is a\nthin shim:\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/fieldmanager.go\n```\n\nIt re-exports `FieldManager = internal.FieldManager` and provides\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` and `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` as the two construction\npaths. The only difference between them is which `structuredMergeManager` is\ninstantiated internally (see \u00a72.3).\n\n### 2.3 The Manager Decorator Chain\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` in `internal/fieldmanager.go` assembles the live\nchain through nested construction calls:\n\n```\nNewVersionCheckManager(\n  NewLastAppliedUpdater(\n    NewLastAppliedManager(\n      NewProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager(\n        NewCapManagersManager(\n          NewBuildManagerInfoManager(\n            NewManagedFieldsUpdater(\n              NewStripMetaManager(structuredMergeManager)\n            ),\n          ),\n        ),\n      ),\n    ),\n  ),\n)\n```\n\nEach layer is a separate file in\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/`:\n\n| Decorator | File | Purpose |\n|---|---|---|\n| `versionCheckManager` | `versioncheck.go` | Rejects apply requests whose GVK doesn't match the registered kind |\n| `lastAppliedUpdater` | `lastappliedupdater.go` | After a successful apply by `kubectl`, rewrites the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation so it stays consistent with SSA |\n| `lastAppliedManager` | `lastappliedmanager.go` | On the first SSA apply by `kubectl`, if conflicts arise only because of CSA-owned fields, it re-runs the apply with `force=true` to silently upgrade the object |\n| `skipNonAppliedManager` / `probabilistic` | `skipnonapplied.go` | Skips managed-field tracking for updates when `managedFields` is empty (no prior apply)\u2014avoids bootstrapping cost. On creates, probabilistically starts tracking at a configurable rate (default: 100 %) |\n| `capManagersManager` | `capmanagers.go` | Ensures at most `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers` (10) entries from update operations; merges older entries into a versioned bucket named `ancient-changes` |\n| `buildManagerInfoManager` | `buildmanagerinfo.go` | Serializes the human-readable manager name into the JSON manager-identifier key that `managedFields` actually stores |\n| `managedFieldsUpdater` | `managedfieldsupdater.go` | Handles timestamp management: detects whether fields changed and updates the per-manager timestamp; for apply, always sets the timestamp if the object changed |\n| `stripMetaManager` | `stripmeta.go` | Removes fixed metadata paths (`apiVersion`, `kind`, `metadata.name`, `metadata.uid`, etc.) from the managed-fields set so they are never tracked as owned by any manager |\n| `structuredMergeManager` | `structuredmerge.go` | The innermost layer; performs the actual merge via `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` |\n\n### 2.4 `structuredMergeManager` and `TypeConverter`\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/structuredmerge.go`\n\nThis is where the merge actually happens. It holds:\n- A `TypeConverter` (`typeconverter.go`)\u2014converts between `runtime.Object` and\n  the `typed.TypedValue` understood by the `structured-merge-diff` library.\n- A `merge.Updater` from `structured-merge-diff`, configured with:\n  - A `versionConverter` (`versionconverter.go`) so the library can convert\n    objects between API versions during merge.\n  - An `IgnoreFilter` (`resetFields` map) allowing specific API fields to be\n    excluded from field tracking (used by subresource reset logic).\n\nFor Apply calls, `structuredMergeManager.Apply` calls:\n```go\nf.updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion, managed.Fields(), manager, force)\n```\nThe `structured-merge-diff` library handles the three-way merge and returns\nconflict errors as a typed `merge.Conflicts` value.\n\nFor CRDs, `NewDeducedTypeConverter` is used\u2014it infers schema from the object's\nshape rather than requiring OpenAPI models, with the constraint that all lists\nare treated as atomic.\n\n### 2.5 The HTTP Handler Entry Point\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`\n\n`PatchResource` dispatches based on `Content-Type`:\n- `application/apply-patch+yaml` \u2192 `applyPatcher`\n- `application/apply-patch+cbor` \u2192 `applyPatcher` (CBOR, feature-gated)\n- `application/json-patch+json` / `application/merge-patch+json` \u2192 `jsonPatcher`\n- `application/strategic-merge-patch+json` \u2192 `smpPatcher`\n\nOnly `applyPatcher` calls `fieldManager.Apply`. The others call\n`fieldManager.UpdateNoErrors`. The `applyPatcher` also sets\n`forceAllowCreate = true` so an apply to a non-existent object is treated as a\ncreate rather than an error.\n\nThe `applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject` (line 500) illustrates the critical\nSSA path:\n\n```go\npatchObj := &unstructured.Unstructured{Object: map[string]interface{}{}}\np.unmarshalFn(p.patch, &patchObj.Object) // decode the YAML apply configuration\nobj, err := p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, p.options.FieldManager, force)\n```\n\nThe decoded patch is always an unstructured object. The `TypeConverter` inside\n`structuredMergeManager` bridges from unstructured to the typed representation\nneeded by the merge library.\n\n### 2.6 ApplyConfigurations Client Library\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/`\n\nThis is a code-generated library (via `applyconfiguration-gen`) that provides\nstrongly typed Go structs for building apply requests. Every field is a pointer,\nso omitting a field is genuinely absent from the JSON payload, not a zero value.\n\nExample from `core/v1/pod.go`:\n```go\ntype PodApplyConfiguration struct {\n    metav1.TypeMetaApplyConfiguration    `json:\",inline\"`\n    *metav1.ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration `json:\"metadata,omitempty\"`\n    Spec   *PodSpecApplyConfiguration    `json:\"spec,omitempty\"`\n    Status *PodStatusApplyConfiguration  `json:\"status,omitempty\"`\n}\n```\n\nEach type also provides:\n- A constructor (`Pod(name, namespace string)`) that pre-populates `kind` and\n  `apiVersion`.\n- An `ExtractPodFrom(pod, fieldManager, subresource)` function that reads back\n  only the fields currently owned by `fieldManager` from a live object, enabling\n  the _extract/modify/re-apply_ workflow.\n\nThe extraction is powered by `managedfields.ExtractInto`\n(`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/extract.go`), which:\n1. Finds the `ManagedFieldsEntry` for the given field manager (Apply operation\n   only, not Update).\n2. Deserializes `FieldsV1` as a `fieldpath.Set`.\n3. Calls `typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves())` to retrieve only the leaf\n   fields from the typed object.\n4. Converts the result back to the apply-configuration struct via\n   `runtime.DefaultUnstructuredConverter.FromUnstructured`.\n\nThe `internal.go` file in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/internal/`\nembeds the OpenAPI schema used to parse objects into typed values. This is the\nparser that `ExtractPodFrom` references via `internal.Parser().Type(...)`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\nHere is the path of an SSA apply request from client to etcd:\n\n### Step 1 \u2014 Client builds and sends the apply configuration\n\nUsing the typed client:\n```go\nhpaApply := autoscalingv1.HorizontalPodAutoscaler(\"hpa-name\", \"default\").\n    WithSpec(autoscalingv1.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec().\n        WithMinReplicas(2).WithMaxReplicas(10))\nclient.AutoscalingV1().HorizontalPodAutoscalers(\"default\").\n    Apply(ctx, hpaApply, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"mycontroller\", Force: true})\n```\n\nThe client marshals the apply configuration to JSON/YAML and issues:\n```\nPATCH /apis/autoscaling/v1/namespaces/default/horizontalpodautoscalers/hpa-name\nContent-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml\n?fieldManager=mycontroller&force=true\n```\n\n### Step 2 \u2014 HTTP routing selects the patch handler\n\n`PatchResource` in `patch.go:68` reads the `Content-Type`. Seeing\n`application/apply-patch+yaml`, it selects `applyPatcher` and sets\n`forceAllowCreate = true`.\n\nThe patch bytes are decoded (line 510):\n```go\npatchObj := &unstructured.Unstructured{Object: map[string]interface{}{}}\nyaml.Unmarshal(p.patch, &patchObj.Object)\n```\n\n### Step 3 \u2014 Optimistic concurrency retry loop\n\n`patcher.patchResource` calls `p.restPatcher.Update(...)` which internally\ncalls `store.GuaranteedUpdate`. This is the standard etcd optimistic locking\nloop: read the live object, call the transformer (our `applyPatch` and\n`applyAdmission` functions), write with the old `resourceVersion` as a\nprecondition, retry on conflict.\n\n### Step 4 \u2014 `applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject` (patch.go:500)\n\nFor an existing object: calls `p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, fieldManager, force)`.\n\nFor a non-existent object (create-on-apply): `applyPatcher.createNewObject`\ncreates an empty object and calls `applyPatchToCurrentObject` against it.\n\n### Step 5 \u2014 `FieldManager.Apply` (internal/fieldmanager.go:183)\n\n1. Reads `managedFields` from the _live_ object via `DecodeManagedFields`.\n2. Delegates to the `Manager` chain.\n\n### Step 6 \u2014 The Manager chain processes the request\n\nCall order (outermost \u2192 innermost):\n\n1. **`versionCheckManager`**: Verifies that `patchObj.GVK == expected GVK`.\n2. **`lastAppliedUpdater`** (Apply only; Update is pass-through): After a\n   successful apply, if manager is `\"kubectl\"` and the annotation exists,\n   re-serializes the applied object into the `last-applied-configuration`\n   annotation for backward compatibility.\n3. **`lastAppliedManager`** (Apply by `\"kubectl\"` only): Tries the apply; if\n   it gets conflicts, checks whether they are all within fields claimed by the\n   old CSA annotation. If so, re-runs with `force=true`\u2014an automatic, silent\n   upgrade from CSA to SSA. For non-`\"kubectl\"` managers, this is a pass-through.\n4. **`skipNonAppliedManager`**: If `managedFields` is empty and the object\n   already has a UID (i.e., it's an update, not a create), skips managed field\n   tracking entirely. For Apply with empty managed fields, synthesizes an initial\n   `Update` entry attributed to `\"before-first-apply\"` to represent all existing\n   fields before they become tracked.\n5. **`capManagersManager`** (Update only): After the inner apply completes,\n   consolidates update-operation entries to \u2264 10 total by merging the oldest\n   entries into `\"ancient-changes\"` buckets keyed by API version.\n6. **`buildManagerInfoManager`**: Serializes the manager name into a JSON key\n   that includes `{manager, operation, apiVersion, subresource}`.\n7. **`managedFieldsUpdater`**: For Update: computes field ownership diff using\n   a sentinel manager (`\"current-operation\"`), then assigns the real manager\n   name and sets the timestamp. For Apply: sets the timestamp after a successful\n   merge.\n8. **`stripMetaManager`**: Post-processes the resulting `ManagedFields` map to\n   remove the pre-defined set of never-tracked paths.\n9. **`structuredMergeManager`**: Performs the actual structured merge:\n   - Converts live and patch objects to `typed.TypedValue` via `TypeConverter`.\n   - Calls `updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion, managed.Fields(), manager, force)`.\n   - The `structured-merge-diff` library computes the three-way merge and\n     returns the new object plus updated ownership sets.\n   - If `force=false` and there are conflicts, returns `merge.Conflicts`.\n   - Converts the merged `TypedValue` back to a `runtime.Object`.\n   - Applies defaults via `objectDefaulter.Default(newObj)`.\n   - Converts back to the hub (internal) version.\n\n### Step 7 \u2014 Conflict error conversion (internal/fieldmanager.go:198)\n\nIf the chain returns `merge.Conflicts`:\n```go\nif conflicts, ok := err.(merge.Conflicts); ok {\n    return nil, NewConflictError(conflicts)\n}\n```\n\n`NewConflictError` in `internal/conflict.go:33` converts each conflict entry\ninto a `metav1.StatusCause` with type `FieldManagerConflict`, populating\n`.Field` with the full field path and `.Message` with the conflicting manager\nname.\n\n### Step 8 \u2014 Managed fields encoded and written\n\nAfter the chain succeeds, `FieldManager.Apply` calls\n`EncodeObjectManagedFields(object, managed)` to serialize the updated\n`ManagedFields` back onto `metadata.managedFields`.\n\n### Step 9 \u2014 Admission and storage\n\nAdmission webhooks run via `applyAdmission`. The patched object is then written\nto etcd via the registry. The `IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer`\n(`fieldmanager/equality.go:114`) runs as a storage transformer: if the managed\nfields differ only in timestamps and the rest of the object is identical to the\nlive version, it rolls back the timestamp updates so that a no-op apply does not\nbump `resourceVersion`.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Conflict Handling\n\n### What triggers a conflict\n\nA conflict occurs during an Apply operation when the patch object specifies a\nfield value that is different from the live value, _and_ that field is currently\nowned by a different manager (either an Apply-type or Update-type entry in\n`managedFields`).\n\nThe `structured-merge-diff` library is the authoritative judge. It performs a\nthree-way comparison (intended state in patch, current state in live object,\npreviously applied state for this manager) and surfaces fields where ownership\ndisputes arise.\n\n### Conflict response format\n\nThe HTTP response is `409 Conflict`, body:\n```json\n{\n  \"status\": \"Failure\",\n  \"reason\": \"Conflict\",\n  \"details\": {\n    \"causes\": [\n      {\n        \"reason\": \"FieldManagerConflict\",\n        \"message\": \"conflict with \\\"other-controller\\\"\",\n        \"field\": \".spec.replicas\"\n      }\n    ]\n  }\n}\n```\n\nThe full conflict message is built in `internal/conflict.go:45`:\n- Single conflict: `\"Apply failed with 1 conflict: conflict with \\\"X\\\": .spec.replicas\"`.\n- Multiple conflicts grouped by manager.\n\n### Resolving conflicts\n\n**Option 1 \u2014 Force (`force=true`)**: The applying manager takes ownership of all\nconflicting fields. Existing owners lose the contested fields from their\n`managedFields` entry. Use this for authoritative controllers.\n\n**Option 2 \u2014 Remove the field from the apply configuration**: The applying\nmanager stops expressing intent for that field. The existing owner retains it.\n\n**Option 3 \u2014 Out-of-band coordination**: Two managers agree on field ownership\nby convention (e.g., one manages spec, another manages status).\n\n**Option 4 \u2014 CSA-to-SSA upgrade path**: When the conflict is due to a\n`kubectl-client-side-apply` or similar CSA manager, `UpgradeManagedFields` from\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/csaupgrade/upgrade.go` can merge those\nUpdate entries into an SSA Apply entry in a single JSON patch, before the first\nSSA apply is attempted.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Field Ownership Model and Data Structures\n\n### `ManagedFieldsEntry`\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1/types.go\ntype ManagedFieldsEntry struct {\n    Manager     string                  // human-readable name\n    Operation   ManagedFieldsOperationType // \"Apply\" or \"Update\"\n    APIVersion  string                  // for Update managers (not Apply)\n    Time        *Time\n    FieldsType  string                  // always \"FieldsV1\"\n    FieldsV1    *FieldsV1               // JSON-encoded trie of field paths\n    Subresource string\n}\n```\n\nThe internal manager identifier key stored in `fieldpath.ManagedFields` is the\nJSON-serialized form of `{manager, operation, subresource}` for Apply, plus\n`{apiVersion}` for Update (built in `buildmanagerinfo.go:63`). This means:\n- An Apply manager always has the same key regardless of API version (it tracks\n  ownership across version upgrades).\n- An Update manager has a different key per API version.\n\n### `FieldsV1` trie\n\n`FieldsV1` encodes a set of field paths as a compact prefix-tree (trie). The\nformat is defined by `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6/fieldpath`. A `.`\nentry in the trie means \"this node itself is owned\"; nested keys represent\nsub-paths. For list elements, the key is the serialized key fields (the\nmerge-key values).\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### Performance\n\n**Conversion cost**: Every apply operation converts the live object and the\npatch object to `typed.TypedValue` using the OpenAPI schema. For complex schemas\n(large CRDs, built-in types like `Pod`), this conversion is non-trivial. The\nschema is pre-parsed and indexed by GVK in `typeconverter.go:116` at startup,\nso per-request cost is parsing JSON/YAML + schema validation.\n\n**Managed fields size**: Each manager occupies one entry in `managedFields` plus\nthe encoded trie. A large number of managers or very many fields per manager\ninflates object size. The `capManagersManager` limits update-manager entries to\n10, and the fallback behavior when etcd rejects an oversized object is to strip\n`managedFields` entirely and retry (`patch.go:713\u2013724`):\n```go\nif isTooLargeError(err) && p.patchType != types.ApplyYAMLPatchType {\n    accessor.SetManagedFields(nil)\n    result, err = requestFunc()\n}\n```\nNote that Apply requests are _never_ retried with stripped managed fields, which\nmeans an apply request can fail with a size error that a regular update would\nsilently recover from.\n\n**No-op apply optimization**: `IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer` in\n`fieldmanager/equality.go` prevents a no-content apply from bumping\n`resourceVersion`. The check runs on every apply and requires two full-object\nequality checks (fast path: compare managed fields modulo timestamps; slow path:\ncompare entire objects). Under high apply frequency (e.g., controllers that\nreconcile every second), this can add measurable CPU cost.\n\n**Probabilistic tracking on create** (`DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability = 1`):\nBy default, every new object immediately starts tracking managed fields. Setting\nthis below 1.0 is a knob to reduce overhead for high-create workloads (e.g.,\nPods created and deleted rapidly). At 0.0, tracking only begins after the first\napply (the original `NewSkipNonAppliedManager` behavior).\n\n### Reliability\n\n**The `UpdateNoErrors` contract**: Non-apply write paths (PUT, strategic merge\npatch, JSON patch) call `UpdateNoErrors`. If the managed field computation fails\nfor any reason (e.g., schema mismatch, corrupt managed fields on the object),\nthe error is logged at most once per second and the write proceeds with\n`managedFields` cleared. This means managed field information can silently\ndisappear, making it unreliable for authorization or audit purposes without\nadditional safeguards.\n\n**Managed field re-population**: If `managedFields` is empty or missing, the\nnext apply by any manager initializes it from scratch via `skipNonAppliedManager`,\nattributing all existing fields to `\"before-first-apply\"`. This prevents the\nfirst applier from conflicts with pre-existing fields.\n\n**Version conversion errors**: The `versionConverter.IsMissingVersionError`\nmethod (`versionconverter.go:101`) treats both `NotRegisteredError` and\n`noCorrespondingTypeError` as \"missing version\" rather than fatal errors. This\nallows the merge library to skip conversion for unmapped versions (important for\nmulti-version CRDs where not all versions may be registered simultaneously).\n\n### Maintainability\n\n**Code generation**: The entire `applyconfigurations` directory is generated\ncode (`applyconfiguration-gen`). Any changes to API types require re-running the\ngenerator. The generated `internal.go` contains the embedded OpenAPI schema\nused for extraction; it must also be regenerated when APIs change.\n\n**Decorator chain fragility**: The specific ordering of the Manager decorators\nin `NewDefaultFieldManager` is semantically critical. For example,\n`lastAppliedUpdater` must wrap `lastAppliedManager` (not the other way around)\nbecause `lastAppliedManager` may re-run apply with force, and only after\n_that_ successful apply should the annotation be updated. Similarly,\n`stripMetaManager` must be innermost (so it strips after the merge) but outside\n`managedFieldsUpdater` (so the timestamp update is not confused by the stripped\nfields). These invariants are not enforced by the type system and are documented\nonly in comments.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Extension Points and Customization\n\n### Custom FieldManager name\n\nEvery actor (controller, operator, kubectl) must supply a non-empty\n`fieldManager` string. The name must be unique per logical owner. Names are\nfree-form strings; the convention is kebab-case tool names.\n\nTo opt out of the `lastAppliedManager` and `lastAppliedUpdater` behaviors, use\nany manager name other than `\"kubectl\"` (hard-coded in both\n`lastappliedmanager.go:63` and `lastappliedupdater.go:58`).\n\n### `resetFields` / `IgnoreFilter`\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` accepts a `resetFields map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter`\nparameter. This filter is passed to `merge.Updater.IgnoreFilter` and tells the\n`structured-merge-diff` library to exclude certain field paths from ownership\ntracking entirely. It is used by subresource handlers (e.g., status) to prevent\napply from ever claiming ownership of fields that the subresource resets.\n\nExample: The `status` subresource might set `resetFields` to filter out\n`.spec.*` paths, ensuring that a status-subresource apply can never affect spec\nfield ownership.\n\n### `ScaleHandler`\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/scalehandler.go`\n\n`ScaleHandler` translates managed-field entries between a root resource (e.g.,\nDeployment) and the `/scale` subresource. Because the `scale` subresource uses\nthe `autoscaling/v1.Scale` schema\u2014with `spec.replicas` at a different path than\nthe parent\u2014`ToSubresource` and `ToParent` perform a path remapping. This is\nrequired so that the field manager that owns `spec.replicas` in a Deployment is\ncorrectly reflected as owning `spec.replicas` in the Scale object, and vice\nversa.\n\n### CRD FieldManager\n\n`NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` uses `NewCRDStructuredMergeManager`, which uses\n`newCRDVersionConverter` instead of `newVersionConverter`. The CRD converter\nalways routes through the single hub version (the storage version) rather than\nKubernetes' internal hub group. For CRDs with no schema, `NewDeducedTypeConverter`\nis used, which treats all lists as atomic\u2014no granular list-item ownership.\n\n### Admission integration\n\n`fieldmanager.NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` in\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`\nwraps the admission chain to validate that mutation webhooks do not break\nmanaged field invariants. If an admission webhook modifies `managedFields`\nin a way that is structurally invalid (e.g., unknown `fieldsType`), the\nvalidation layer rejects the write.\n\n### CSA-to-SSA migration utility\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/csaupgrade/upgrade.go`\n\n`UpgradeManagedFields(obj, csaManagerNames, ssaManagerName)` rewrites the\n`managedFields` on an object in memory: it merges all Update entries whose\n`.Manager` matches any name in `csaManagerNames` into a single Apply entry\nnamed `ssaManagerName`. The helper `UpgradeManagedFieldsPatch` returns a\nminimal JSON patch that can be sent to the API server, including a\n`resourceVersion` test to prevent races.\n\n**Risk**: This is a one-way, irreversible operation. Information about which\nspecific fields each CSA manager controlled is lost after the merge.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Failure Modes and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### Conflict error on first SSA apply\n\nWhen an object has only ever been written via Update operations (or CSA), its\n`managedFields` may be empty or contain only Update entries. The first apply\nby a new manager can produce conflicts if the live object has fields in the\napply configuration that another Update manager owns. The automatic upgrade\nvia `lastAppliedManager` only helps the `kubectl` manager. All other managers\nmust either use `force=true` or use `UpgradeManagedFields` as a preparatory\nstep.\n\n### Silent managed-field loss\n\nThe `UpdateNoErrors` fallback silently drops `managedFields` on any internal\nerror. Additionally, when an object exceeds the etcd size limit, non-apply\nrequests strip `managedFields` and retry. Operators relying on `managedFields`\nfor any purpose (access control, audit) should be aware of these loss scenarios.\n\n### Manager count explosion\n\nWithout the `capManagersManager` cap, every deployment pipeline that applies\ndistinct field-manager names would accumulate entries indefinitely. The cap at\n10 Update entries prevents this but merges older entries into `\"ancient-changes\"`,\nlosing the attribution granularity. Apply managers are not subject to this cap.\n\n### API version skew\n\nApply requests must match the GVK exactly (`versionCheckManager`). A client\nusing `apps/v1beta1` while the server has migrated to `apps/v1` will receive\na `400 Bad Request`. Managed-field entries for Update managers include the API\nversion as part of their key, so a version migration can leave stale entries\nunder old version keys.\n\n### Subresource isolation\n\nThe `isSubresource` flag in `FieldManager.Update` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:123`)\ncauses subresource updates (e.g., status writes) to always use the live object's\n`managedFields` rather than whatever the request body contains. This prevents a\nstatus writer from accidentally overwriting the root object's field ownership.\n\n---\n\n## 9. File and Directory Map\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/` | Public API: `FieldManager`, `ExtractInto`, `ScaleHandler`, `TypeConverter` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/` | All internal Manager decorators and merge logic |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go` | `FieldManager` struct and its `Apply`/`Update`/`UpdateNoErrors` methods |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/manager.go` | `Manager` and `Managed` interfaces |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/structuredmerge.go` | Core merge logic via `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/managedfields.go` | Encode/decode `managedFields` \u2194 `fieldpath.ManagedFields` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/conflict.go` | Convert `merge.Conflicts` to `StatusError` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/typeconverter.go` | Bridge between `runtime.Object` and `typed.TypedValue`; schema indexing |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/versionconverter.go` | Bridge between Kubernetes version conversion and `merge.Converter` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/capmanagers.go` | Caps update-manager count at `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/skipnonapplied.go` | Skips tracking for updates when no prior apply exists |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/lastappliedmanager.go` | Upgrades CSA-conflicted applies for `kubectl` manager |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/lastappliedupdater.go` | Keeps `last-applied-configuration` annotation in sync with SSA |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/stripmeta.go` | Strips non-trackable metadata paths from managed fields |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/buildmanagerinfo.go` | Serializes manager identity into JSON key |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/managedfieldsupdater.go` | Timestamp management for Update and Apply |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/versioncheck.go` | Validates GVK of the applied object |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/extract.go` | `ExtractInto`: pull back only manager-owned fields |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/scalehandler.go` | Path translation for `/scale` subresource |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` | HTTP patch handler; maps `runtime.Object` to its apply configuration type |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/csaupgrade/upgrade.go` | `UpgradeManagedFields` / `UpgradeManagedFieldsPatch` for CSA\u2192SSA migration |\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"

{
  "content": "# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and ApplyConfigurations: A Deep Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is a Kubernetes API mechanism introduced to replace the\nclient-side `kubectl apply` workflow with a server-enforced, field-ownership\nmodel. Instead of the client computing a three-way diff and sending a strategic\nmerge patch, the client sends a _declarative intent_\u2014a partial object\u2014and the\nserver is responsible for merging it with the live object, tracking ownership of\neach field, and detecting conflicts between competing actors.\n\n**What the subsystem does:**\n\n- Accepts apply requests (`PATCH` with `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml`)\n  and merge-patch/update requests.\n- Determines which fields are owned by which _field manager_ (identified by the\n  `fieldManager` query parameter) and records ownership in\n  `metadata.managedFields`.\n- Detects conflicts\u2014when two managers claim the same field with different\n  intended values\u2014and either returns a `409 Conflict` or forces through the\n  change when `force=true`.\n- Prunes fields that a manager previously owned but no longer declares in its\n  applied configuration.\n- Maintains backward compatibility with the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration`\n  annotation used by client-side apply.\n\n**Boundaries:**\n\n- The subsystem lives within the API server. The client's only job is to\n  produce an _apply configuration_\u2014a partial, pointer-heavy struct representation\n  of the intended object state.\n- Upstream: HTTP routing in `pkg/endpoints` passes PATCH requests to\n  `PatchResource` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`.\n- Downstream: After field management completes, the resulting object is\n  validated by admission webhooks and written to etcd via the registry layer.\n- Out of scope: The strategic merge patch algorithm used by classical `kubectl apply`\n  (client-side apply) is an entirely separate code path and does not run for SSA requests.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\nThe SSA subsystem is layered across three staging modules:\n\n| Module | Responsibility |\n|---|---|\n| `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields` | Core FieldManager orchestrator and public API |\n| `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal` | The actual merge/tracking logic, implemented as a chain of Manager decorators |\n| `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers` | HTTP entry point; ties FieldManager into the patch handler |\n| `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager` | Admission validation and noop-timestamp optimization |\n| `k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations` | Generated client-side types used to build apply requests |\n| `k8s.io/client-go/util/csaupgrade` | Utility for migrating CSA-managed objects to SSA |\n\n### 2.1 The `Manager` Interface\n\nThe central abstraction is the `Manager` interface in\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/manager.go`:\n\n```go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n    Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, fieldManager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n}\n```\n\n- **`Update`** is called for all non-apply write operations (PUT, strategic merge\n  patch, JSON patch). It only updates the field-ownership bookkeeping; the\n  object merge was already performed by the caller.\n- **`Apply`** is called for SSA requests. It both merges the applied configuration\n  into the live object and updates ownership.\n\nThe `Managed` interface (`manager.go`) groups a `fieldpath.ManagedFields` map\nfrom `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` with per-manager timestamps. This is\nthe in-memory representation of `metadata.managedFields`.\n\n### 2.2 The `FieldManager` Facade\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go`\nwraps a `Manager` chain and is the object exposed to the HTTP handler. Its\nexported methods:\n\n- `Update(liveObj, newObj, managerName)` \u2014 decodes managed fields from the\n  request, delegates to the chain, then re-encodes them back onto the result.\n- `Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, managerName, force)` \u2014 reads managed fields from\n  the live object (never from the applied patch, which must not contain them),\n  delegates to the chain, then re-encodes.\n- `UpdateNoErrors` \u2014 same as `Update` but swallows errors, clearing\n  `managedFields` rather than propagating the failure. Used for non-apply paths\n  where managed-field tracking is best-effort.\n\nThe public package `managedfields` (`fieldmanager.go` at the public level) is a\nthin shim:\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/fieldmanager.go\n```\n\nIt re-exports `FieldManager = internal.FieldManager` and provides\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` and `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` as the two construction\npaths. The only difference between them is which `structuredMergeManager` is\ninstantiated internally (see \u00a72.3).\n\n### 2.3 The Manager Decorator Chain\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` in `internal/fieldmanager.go` assembles the live\nchain through nested construction calls:\n\n```\nNewVersionCheckManager(\n  NewLastAppliedUpdater(\n    NewLastAppliedManager(\n      NewProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager(\n        NewCapManagersManager(\n          NewBuildManagerInfoManager(\n            NewManagedFieldsUpdater(\n              NewStripMetaManager(structuredMergeManager)\n            ),\n          ),\n        ),\n      ),\n    ),\n  ),\n)\n```\n\nEach layer is a separate file in\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/`:\n\n| Decorator | File | Purpose |\n|---|---|---|\n| `versionCheckManager` | `versioncheck.go` | Rejects apply requests whose GVK doesn't match the registered kind |\n| `lastAppliedUpdater` | `lastappliedupdater.go` | After a successful apply by `kubectl`, rewrites the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation so it stays consistent with SSA |\n| `lastAppliedManager` | `lastappliedmanager.go` | On the first SSA apply by `kubectl`, if conflicts arise only because of CSA-owned fields, it re-runs the apply with `force=true` to silently upgrade the object |\n| `skipNonAppliedManager` / `probabilistic` | `skipnonapplied.go` | Skips managed-field tracking for updates when `managedFields` is empty (no prior apply)\u2014avoids bootstrapping cost. On creates, probabilistically starts tracking at a configurable rate (default: 100 %) |\n| `capManagersManager` | `capmanagers.go` | Ensures at most `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers` (10) entries from update operations; merges older entries into a versioned bucket named `ancient-changes` |\n| `buildManagerInfoManager` | `buildmanagerinfo.go` | Serializes the human-readable manager name into the JSON manager-identifier key that `managedFields` actually stores |\n| `managedFieldsUpdater` | `managedfieldsupdater.go` | Handles timestamp management: detects whether fields changed and updates the per-manager timestamp; for apply, always sets the timestamp if the object changed |\n| `stripMetaManager` | `stripmeta.go` | Removes fixed metadata paths (`apiVersion`, `kind`, `metadata.name`, `metadata.uid`, etc.) from the managed-fields set so they are never tracked as owned by any manager |\n| `structuredMergeManager` | `structuredmerge.go` | The innermost layer; performs the actual merge via `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` |\n\n### 2.4 `structuredMergeManager` and `TypeConverter`\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/structuredmerge.go`\n\nThis is where the merge actually happens. It holds:\n- A `TypeConverter` (`typeconverter.go`)\u2014converts between `runtime.Object` and\n  the `typed.TypedValue` understood by the `structured-merge-diff` library.\n- A `merge.Updater` from `structured-merge-diff`, configured with:\n  - A `versionConverter` (`versionconverter.go`) so the library can convert\n    objects between API versions during merge.\n  - An `IgnoreFilter` (`resetFields` map) allowing specific API fields to be\n    excluded from field tracking (used by subresource reset logic).\n\nFor Apply calls, `structuredMergeManager.Apply` calls:\n```go\nf.updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion, managed.Fields(), manager, force)\n```\nThe `structured-merge-diff` library handles the three-way merge and returns\nconflict errors as a typed `merge.Conflicts` value.\n\nFor CRDs, `NewDeducedTypeConverter` is used\u2014it infers schema from the object's\nshape rather than requiring OpenAPI models, with the constraint that all lists\nare treated as atomic.\n\n### 2.5 The HTTP Handler Entry Point\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`\n\n`PatchResource` dispatches based on `Content-Type`:\n- `application/apply-patch+yaml` \u2192 `applyPatcher`\n- `application/apply-patch+cbor` \u2192 `applyPatcher` (CBOR, feature-gated)\n- `application/json-patch+json` / `application/merge-patch+json` \u2192 `jsonPatcher`\n- `application/strategic-merge-patch+json` \u2192 `smpPatcher`\n\nOnly `applyPatcher` calls `fieldManager.Apply`. The others call\n`fieldManager.UpdateNoErrors`. The `applyPatcher` also sets\n`forceAllowCreate = true` so an apply to a non-existent object is treated as a\ncreate rather than an error.\n\nThe `applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject` (line 500) illustrates the critical\nSSA path:\n\n```go\npatchObj := &unstructured.Unstructured{Object: map[string]interface{}{}}\np.unmarshalFn(p.patch, &patchObj.Object) // decode the YAML apply configuration\nobj, err := p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, p.options.FieldManager, force)\n```\n\nThe decoded patch is always an unstructured object. The `TypeConverter` inside\n`structuredMergeManager` bridges from unstructured to the typed representation\nneeded by the merge library.\n\n### 2.6 ApplyConfigurations Client Library\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/`\n\nThis is a code-generated library (via `applyconfiguration-gen`) that provides\nstrongly typed Go structs for building apply requests. Every field is a pointer,\nso omitting a field is genuinely absent from the JSON payload, not a zero value.\n\nExample from `core/v1/pod.go`:\n```go\ntype PodApplyConfiguration struct {\n    metav1.TypeMetaApplyConfiguration    `json:\",inline\"`\n    *metav1.ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration `json:\"metadata,omitempty\"`\n    Spec   *PodSpecApplyConfiguration    `json:\"spec,omitempty\"`\n    Status *PodStatusApplyConfiguration  `json:\"status,omitempty\"`\n}\n```\n\nEach type also provides:\n- A constructor (`Pod(name, namespace string)`) that pre-populates `kind` and\n  `apiVersion`.\n- An `ExtractPodFrom(pod, fieldManager, subresource)` function that reads back\n  only the fields currently owned by `fieldManager` from a live object, enabling\n  the _extract/modify/re-apply_ workflow.\n\nThe extraction is powered by `managedfields.ExtractInto`\n(`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/extract.go`), which:\n1. Finds the `ManagedFieldsEntry` for the given field manager (Apply operation\n   only, not Update).\n2. Deserializes `FieldsV1` as a `fieldpath.Set`.\n3. Calls `typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves())` to retrieve only the leaf\n   fields from the typed object.\n4. Converts the result back to the apply-configuration struct via\n   `runtime.DefaultUnstructuredConverter.FromUnstructured`.\n\nThe `internal.go` file in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/internal/`\nembeds the OpenAPI schema used to parse objects into typed values. This is the\nparser that `ExtractPodFrom` references via `internal.Parser().Type(...)`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\nHere is the path of an SSA apply request from client to etcd:\n\n### Step 1 \u2014 Client builds and sends the apply configuration\n\nUsing the typed client:\n```go\nhpaApply := autoscalingv1.HorizontalPodAutoscaler(\"hpa-name\", \"default\").\n    WithSpec(autoscalingv1.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec().\n        WithMinReplicas(2).WithMaxReplicas(10))\nclient.AutoscalingV1().HorizontalPodAutoscalers(\"default\").\n    Apply(ctx, hpaApply, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"mycontroller\", Force: true})\n```\n\nThe client marshals the apply configuration to JSON/YAML and issues:\n```\nPATCH /apis/autoscaling/v1/namespaces/default/horizontalpodautoscalers/hpa-name\nContent-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml\n?fieldManager=mycontroller&force=true\n```\n\n### Step 2 \u2014 HTTP routing selects the patch handler\n\n`PatchResource` in `patch.go:68` reads the `Content-Type`. Seeing\n`application/apply-patch+yaml`, it selects `applyPatcher` and sets\n`forceAllowCreate = true`.\n\nThe patch bytes are decoded (line 510):\n```go\npatchObj := &unstructured.Unstructured{Object: map[string]interface{}{}}\nyaml.Unmarshal(p.patch, &patchObj.Object)\n```\n\n### Step 3 \u2014 Optimistic concurrency retry loop\n\n`patcher.patchResource` calls `p.restPatcher.Update(...)` which internally\ncalls `store.GuaranteedUpdate`. This is the standard etcd optimistic locking\nloop: read the live object, call the transformer (our `applyPatch` and\n`applyAdmission` functions), write with the old `resourceVersion` as a\nprecondition, retry on conflict.\n\n### Step 4 \u2014 `applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject` (patch.go:500)\n\nFor an existing object: calls `p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, fieldManager, force)`.\n\nFor a non-existent object (create-on-apply): `applyPatcher.createNewObject`\ncreates an empty object and calls `applyPatchToCurrentObject` against it.\n\n### Step 5 \u2014 `FieldManager.Apply` (internal/fieldmanager.go:183)\n\n1. Reads `managedFields` from the _live_ object via `DecodeManagedFields`.\n2. Delegates to the `Manager` chain.\n\n### Step 6 \u2014 The Manager chain processes the request\n\nCall order (outermost \u2192 innermost):\n\n1. **`versionCheckManager`**: Verifies that `patchObj.GVK == expected GVK`.\n2. **`lastAppliedUpdater`** (Apply only; Update is pass-through): After a\n   successful apply, if manager is `\"kubectl\"` and the annotation exists,\n   re-serializes the applied object into the `last-applied-configuration`\n   annotation for backward compatibility.\n3. **`lastAppliedManager`** (Apply by `\"kubectl\"` only): Tries the apply; if\n   it gets conflicts, checks whether they are all within fields claimed by the\n   old CSA annotation. If so, re-runs with `force=true`\u2014an automatic, silent\n   upgrade from CSA to SSA. For non-`\"kubectl\"` managers, this is a pass-through.\n4. **`skipNonAppliedManager`**: If `managedFields` is empty and the object\n   already has a UID (i.e., it's an update, not a create), skips managed field\n   tracking entirely. For Apply with empty managed fields, synthesizes an initial\n   `Update` entry attributed to `\"before-first-apply\"` to represent all existing\n   fields before they become tracked.\n5. **`capManagersManager`** (Update only): After the inner apply completes,\n   consolidates update-operation entries to \u2264 10 total by merging the oldest\n   entries into `\"ancient-changes\"` buckets keyed by API version.\n6. **`buildManagerInfoManager`**: Serializes the manager name into a JSON key\n   that includes `{manager, operation, apiVersion, subresource}`.\n7. **`managedFieldsUpdater`**: For Update: computes field ownership diff using\n   a sentinel manager (`\"current-operation\"`), then assigns the real manager\n   name and sets the timestamp. For Apply: sets the timestamp after a successful\n   merge.\n8. **`stripMetaManager`**: Post-processes the resulting `ManagedFields` map to\n   remove the pre-defined set of never-tracked paths.\n9. **`structuredMergeManager`**: Performs the actual structured merge:\n   - Converts live and patch objects to `typed.TypedValue` via `TypeConverter`.\n   - Calls `updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion, managed.Fields(), manager, force)`.\n   - The `structured-merge-diff` library computes the three-way merge and\n     returns the new object plus updated ownership sets.\n   - If `force=false` and there are conflicts, returns `merge.Conflicts`.\n   - Converts the merged `TypedValue` back to a `runtime.Object`.\n   - Applies defaults via `objectDefaulter.Default(newObj)`.\n   - Converts back to the hub (internal) version.\n\n### Step 7 \u2014 Conflict error conversion (internal/fieldmanager.go:198)\n\nIf the chain returns `merge.Conflicts`:\n```go\nif conflicts, ok := err.(merge.Conflicts); ok {\n    return nil, NewConflictError(conflicts)\n}\n```\n\n`NewConflictError` in `internal/conflict.go:33` converts each conflict entry\ninto a `metav1.StatusCause` with type `FieldManagerConflict`, populating\n`.Field` with the full field path and `.Message` with the conflicting manager\nname.\n\n### Step 8 \u2014 Managed fields encoded and written\n\nAfter the chain succeeds, `FieldManager.Apply` calls\n`EncodeObjectManagedFields(object, managed)` to serialize the updated\n`ManagedFields` back onto `metadata.managedFields`.\n\n### Step 9 \u2014 Admission and storage\n\nAdmission webhooks run via `applyAdmission`. The patched object is then written\nto etcd via the registry. The `IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer`\n(`fieldmanager/equality.go:114`) runs as a storage transformer: if the managed\nfields differ only in timestamps and the rest of the object is identical to the\nlive version, it rolls back the timestamp updates so that a no-op apply does not\nbump `resourceVersion`.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Conflict Handling\n\n### What triggers a conflict\n\nA conflict occurs during an Apply operation when the patch object specifies a\nfield value that is different from the live value, _and_ that field is currently\nowned by a different manager (either an Apply-type or Update-type entry in\n`managedFields`).\n\nThe `structured-merge-diff` library is the authoritative judge. It performs a\nthree-way comparison (intended state in patch, current state in live object,\npreviously applied state for this manager) and surfaces fields where ownership\ndisputes arise.\n\n### Conflict response format\n\nThe HTTP response is `409 Conflict`, body:\n```json\n{\n  \"status\": \"Failure\",\n  \"reason\": \"Conflict\",\n  \"details\": {\n    \"causes\": [\n      {\n        \"reason\": \"FieldManagerConflict\",\n        \"message\": \"conflict with \\\"other-controller\\\"\",\n        \"field\": \".spec.replicas\"\n      }\n    ]\n  }\n}\n```\n\nThe full conflict message is built in `internal/conflict.go:45`:\n- Single conflict: `\"Apply failed with 1 conflict: conflict with \\\"X\\\": .spec.replicas\"`.\n- Multiple conflicts grouped by manager.\n\n### Resolving conflicts\n\n**Option 1 \u2014 Force (`force=true`)**: The applying manager takes ownership of all\nconflicting fields. Existing owners lose the contested fields from their\n`managedFields` entry. Use this for authoritative controllers.\n\n**Option 2 \u2014 Remove the field from the apply configuration**: The applying\nmanager stops expressing intent for that field. The existing owner retains it.\n\n**Option 3 \u2014 Out-of-band coordination**: Two managers agree on field ownership\nby convention (e.g., one manages spec, another manages status).\n\n**Option 4 \u2014 CSA-to-SSA upgrade path**: When the conflict is due to a\n`kubectl-client-side-apply` or similar CSA manager, `UpgradeManagedFields` from\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/csaupgrade/upgrade.go` can merge those\nUpdate entries into an SSA Apply entry in a single JSON patch, before the first\nSSA apply is attempted.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Field Ownership Model and Data Structures\n\n### `ManagedFieldsEntry`\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1/types.go\ntype ManagedFieldsEntry struct {\n    Manager     string                  // human-readable name\n    Operation   ManagedFieldsOperationType // \"Apply\" or \"Update\"\n    APIVersion  string                  // for Update managers (not Apply)\n    Time        *Time\n    FieldsType  string                  // always \"FieldsV1\"\n    FieldsV1    *FieldsV1               // JSON-encoded trie of field paths\n    Subresource string\n}\n```\n\nThe internal manager identifier key stored in `fieldpath.ManagedFields` is the\nJSON-serialized form of `{manager, operation, subresource}` for Apply, plus\n`{apiVersion}` for Update (built in `buildmanagerinfo.go:63`). This means:\n- An Apply manager always has the same key regardless of API version (it tracks\n  ownership across version upgrades).\n- An Update manager has a different key per API version.\n\n### `FieldsV1` trie\n\n`FieldsV1` encodes a set of field paths as a compact prefix-tree (trie). The\nformat is defined by `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6/fieldpath`. A `.`\nentry in the trie means \"this node itself is owned\"; nested keys represent\nsub-paths. For list elements, the key is the serialized key fields (the\nmerge-key values).\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### Performance\n\n**Conversion cost**: Every apply operation converts the live object and the\npatch object to `typed.TypedValue` using the OpenAPI schema. For complex schemas\n(large CRDs, built-in types like `Pod`), this conversion is non-trivial. The\nschema is pre-parsed and indexed by GVK in `typeconverter.go:116` at startup,\nso per-request cost is parsing JSON/YAML + schema validation.\n\n**Managed fields size**: Each manager occupies one entry in `managedFields` plus\nthe encoded trie. A large number of managers or very many fields per manager\ninflates object size. The `capManagersManager` limits update-manager entries to\n10, and the fallback behavior when etcd rejects an oversized object is to strip\n`managedFields` entirely and retry (`patch.go:713\u2013724`):\n```go\nif isTooLargeError(err) && p.patchType != types.ApplyYAMLPatchType {\n    accessor.SetManagedFields(nil)\n    result, err = requestFunc()\n}\n```\nNote that Apply requests are _never_ retried with stripped managed fields, which\nmeans an apply request can fail with a size error that a regular update would\nsilently recover from.\n\n**No-op apply optimization**: `IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer` in\n`fieldmanager/equality.go` prevents a no-content apply from bumping\n`resourceVersion`. The check runs on every apply and requires two full-object\nequality checks (fast path: compare managed fields modulo timestamps; slow path:\ncompare entire objects). Under high apply frequency (e.g., controllers that\nreconcile every second), this can add measurable CPU cost.\n\n**Probabilistic tracking on create** (`DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability = 1`):\nBy default, every new object immediately starts tracking managed fields. Setting\nthis below 1.0 is a knob to reduce overhead for high-create workloads (e.g.,\nPods created and deleted rapidly). At 0.0, tracking only begins after the first\napply (the original `NewSkipNonAppliedManager` behavior).\n\n### Reliability\n\n**The `UpdateNoErrors` contract**: Non-apply write paths (PUT, strategic merge\npatch, JSON patch) call `UpdateNoErrors`. If the managed field computation fails\nfor any reason (e.g., schema mismatch, corrupt managed fields on the object),\nthe error is logged at most once per second and the write proceeds with\n`managedFields` cleared. This means managed field information can silently\ndisappear, making it unreliable for authorization or audit purposes without\nadditional safeguards.\n\n**Managed field re-population**: If `managedFields` is empty or missing, the\nnext apply by any manager initializes it from scratch via `skipNonAppliedManager`,\nattributing all existing fields to `\"before-first-apply\"`. This prevents the\nfirst applier from conflicts with pre-existing fields.\n\n**Version conversion errors**: The `versionConverter.IsMissingVersionError`\nmethod (`versionconverter.go:101`) treats both `NotRegisteredError` and\n`noCorrespondingTypeError` as \"missing version\" rather than fatal errors. This\nallows the merge library to skip conversion for unmapped versions (important for\nmulti-version CRDs where not all versions may be registered simultaneously).\n\n### Maintainability\n\n**Code generation**: The entire `applyconfigurations` directory is generated\ncode (`applyconfiguration-gen`). Any changes to API types require re-running the\ngenerator. The generated `internal.go` contains the embedded OpenAPI schema\nused for extraction; it must also be regenerated when APIs change.\n\n**Decorator chain fragility**: The specific ordering of the Manager decorators\nin `NewDefaultFieldManager` is semantically critical. For example,\n`lastAppliedUpdater` must wrap `lastAppliedManager` (not the other way around)\nbecause `lastAppliedManager` may re-run apply with force, and only after\n_that_ successful apply should the annotation be updated. Similarly,\n`stripMetaManager` must be innermost (so it strips after the merge) but outside\n`managedFieldsUpdater` (so the timestamp update is not confused by the stripped\nfields). These invariants are not enforced by the type system and are documented\nonly in comments.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Extension Points and Customization\n\n### Custom FieldManager name\n\nEvery actor (controller, operator, kubectl) must supply a non-empty\n`fieldManager` string. The name must be unique per logical owner. Names are\nfree-form strings; the convention is kebab-case tool names.\n\nTo opt out of the `lastAppliedManager` and `lastAppliedUpdater` behaviors, use\nany manager name other than `\"kubectl\"` (hard-coded in both\n`lastappliedmanager.go:63` and `lastappliedupdater.go:58`).\n\n### `resetFields` / `IgnoreFilter`\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` accepts a `resetFields map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter`\nparameter. This filter is passed to `merge.Updater.IgnoreFilter` and tells the\n`structured-merge-diff` library to exclude certain field paths from ownership\ntracking entirely. It is used by subresource handlers (e.g., status) to prevent\napply from ever claiming ownership of fields that the subresource resets.\n\nExample: The `status` subresource might set `resetFields` to filter out\n`.spec.*` paths, ensuring that a status-subresource apply can never affect spec\nfield ownership.\n\n### `ScaleHandler`\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/scalehandler.go`\n\n`ScaleHandler` translates managed-field entries between a root resource (e.g.,\nDeployment) and the `/scale` subresource. Because the `scale` subresource uses\nthe `autoscaling/v1.Scale` schema\u2014with `spec.replicas` at a different path than\nthe parent\u2014`ToSubresource` and `ToParent` perform a path remapping. This is\nrequired so that the field manager that owns `spec.replicas` in a Deployment is\ncorrectly reflected as owning `spec.replicas` in the Scale object, and vice\nversa.\n\n### CRD FieldManager\n\n`NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` uses `NewCRDStructuredMergeManager`, which uses\n`newCRDVersionConverter` instead of `newVersionConverter`. The CRD converter\nalways routes through the single hub version (the storage version) rather than\nKubernetes' internal hub group. For CRDs with no schema, `NewDeducedTypeConverter`\nis used, which treats all lists as atomic\u2014no granular list-item ownership.\n\n### Admission integration\n\n`fieldmanager.NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` in\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`\nwraps the admission chain to validate that mutation webhooks do not break\nmanaged field invariants. If an admission webhook modifies `managedFields`\nin a way that is structurally invalid (e.g., unknown `fieldsType`), the\nvalidation layer rejects the write.\n\n### CSA-to-SSA migration utility\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/csaupgrade/upgrade.go`\n\n`UpgradeManagedFields(obj, csaManagerNames, ssaManagerName)` rewrites the\n`managedFields` on an object in memory: it merges all Update entries whose\n`.Manager` matches any name in `csaManagerNames` into a single Apply entry\nnamed `ssaManagerName`. The helper `UpgradeManagedFieldsPatch` returns a\nminimal JSON patch that can be sent to the API server, including a\n`resourceVersion` test to prevent races.\n\n**Risk**: This is a one-way, irreversible operation. Information about which\nspecific fields each CSA manager controlled is lost after the merge.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Failure Modes and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### Conflict error on first SSA apply\n\nWhen an object has only ever been written via Update operations (or CSA), its\n`managedFields` may be empty or contain only Update entries. The first apply\nby a new manager can produce conflicts if the live object has fields in the\napply configuration that another Update manager owns. The automatic upgrade\nvia `lastAppliedManager` only helps the `kubectl` manager. All other managers\nmust either use `force=true` or use `UpgradeManagedFields` as a preparatory\nstep.\n\n### Silent managed-field loss\n\nThe `UpdateNoErrors` fallback silently drops `managedFields` on any internal\nerror. Additionally, when an object exceeds the etcd size limit, non-apply\nrequests strip `managedFields` and retry. Operators relying on `managedFields`\nfor any purpose (access control, audit) should be aware of these loss scenarios.\n\n### Manager count explosion\n\nWithout the `capManagersManager` cap, every deployment pipeline that applies\ndistinct field-manager names would accumulate entries indefinitely. The cap at\n10 Update entries prevents this but merges older entries into `\"ancient-changes\"`,\nlosing the attribution granularity. Apply managers are not subject to this cap.\n\n### API version skew\n\nApply requests must match the GVK exactly (`versionCheckManager`). A client\nusing `apps/v1beta1` while the server has migrated to `apps/v1` will receive\na `400 Bad Request`. Managed-field entries for Update managers include the API\nversion as part of their key, so a version migration can leave stale entries\nunder old version keys.\n\n### Subresource isolation\n\nThe `isSubresource` flag in `FieldManager.Update` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:123`)\ncauses subresource updates (e.g., status writes) to always use the live object's\n`managedFields` rather than whatever the request body contains. This prevents a\nstatus writer from accidentally overwriting the root object's field ownership.\n\n---\n\n## 9. File and Directory Map\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/` | Public API: `FieldManager`, `ExtractInto`, `ScaleHandler`, `TypeConverter` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/` | All internal Manager decorators and merge logic |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go` | `FieldManager` struct and its `Apply`/`Update`/`UpdateNoErrors` methods |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/manager.go` | `Manager` and `Managed` interfaces |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/structuredmerge.go` | Core merge logic via `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/managedfields.go` | Encode/decode `managedFields` \u2194 `fieldpath.ManagedFields` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/conflict.go` | Convert `merge.Conflicts` to `StatusError` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/typeconverter.go` | Bridge between `runtime.Object` and `typed.TypedValue`; SSA entry point via `applyPatcher` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/equality.go` | No-op apply timestamp suppression (`IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer`) |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go` | Admission validation wrapper |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Generated typesafe apply-configuration structs |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/utils.go` | `ForObject` helper; # Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and ApplyConfigurations: A Deep Guide

## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries

Server-Side Apply (SSA) is a Kubernetes API mechanism introduced to replace the
client-side `kubectl apply` workflow with a server-enforced, field-ownership
model. Instead of the client computing a three-way diff and sending a strategic
merge patch, the client sends a _declarative intent_—a partial object—and the
server is responsible for merging it with the live object, tracking ownership of
each field, and detecting conflicts between competing actors.

**What the subsystem does:**

- Accepts apply requests (`PATCH` with `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml`)
  and merge-patch/update requests.
- Determines which fields are owned by which _field manager_ (identified by the
  `fieldManager` query parameter) and records ownership in
  `metadata.managedFields`.
- Detects conflicts—when two managers claim the same field with different
  intended values—and either returns a `409 Conflict` or forces through the
  change when `force=true`.
- Prunes fields that a manager previously owned but no longer declares in its
  applied configuration.
- Maintains backward compatibility with the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration`
  annotation used by client-side apply.

**Boundaries:**

- The subsystem lives within the API server. The client's only job is to
  produce an _apply configuration_—a partial, pointer-heavy struct representation
  of the intended object state.
- Upstream: HTTP routing in `pkg/endpoints` passes PATCH requests to
  `PatchResource` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`.
- Downstream: After field management completes, the resulting object is
  validated by admission webhooks and written to etcd via the regis
... (truncated)
